## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics
**Analysis**: This task models the acceleration of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator, where dv_dt depends on position x, velocity v, and possibly time t through nonlinear restoring forces, damping, and/or external driving.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Simple harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator (unforced): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring + damping)
- Quintic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order restoring force)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * x**2 * v (nonlinear damping)
- Driven harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (periodic external force)
- Driven Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (driven cubic oscillator)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x * cos(c1 * t) (time-modulated stiffness)
- Nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * x**2 + c2 * v**3 (position/velocity-dependent damping)
- Softening/hardening spring: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 (asymmetric restoring force)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (cubic velocity nonlinearity)
- Combined nonlinear: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * (1 - x**2) * v (Duffing-Van der Pol hybrid)
- Coulomb-like friction: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * (v**2 + c2)**(-0.5) (regularized dry friction)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x³, x⁵) preserve symmetry of oscillation about equilibrium — expect odd polynomial in x
- Velocity-dependent terms (c*v) indicate energy dissipation or injection — linear damping vs nonlinear damping
- Products of x² and v (x²*v) indicate amplitude-dependent damping characteristic of self-excited oscillators
- Explicit time dependence through sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) indicates external periodic driving forces
- Even powers of x in restoring force (x²) break spatial symmetry and indicate asymmetric potential wells
- Absence of explicit t dependence suggests an autonomous system where energy is conserved or self-regulated
- Cubic velocity terms (v³) appear in Rayleigh-type dissipation modeling air resistance at higher speeds
- Product x*cos(c*t) indicates parametric excitation where the system's natural frequency is modulated

**GT:** `-0.0493727*v³ - 1.02930*(0.02227*t + 1)*x - 1.02930*x + 0.41553*sin(t) - 0.29167*|v|^(1/3)`

Let me simplify the GT:
- `-0.0493727*v³` — cubic in v
- `-1.02930*(0.02227*t + 1)*x - 1.02930*x` = `-1.02930*0.02227*t*x - 1.02930*x - 1.02930*x` = `-0.02293*t*x - 2.05860*x`
- `0.41553*sin(t)` — sine of t
- `-0.29167*|v|^(1/3)` — cube root of absolute value of v

So GT = `-2.05860*x - 0.02293*t*x + 0.41553*sin(t) - 0.0493727*v³ - 0.29167*|v|^(1/3)`

The key basis functions are:
1. `x` (linear)
2. `t*x` (product term)
3. `sin(t)`
4. `v³`
5. `|v|^(1/3)`

Note: `t*x` can be written as `x*cos(0*t)` only if cos is evaluated at 0, but `x*cos(c*t)` with c≠0 gives a different function. However, if we use the product-to-sum or consider `x*cos(c*t)`: when c→0, `cos(c*t)→1`, giving just `c*x`. But we need `t*x`, not just `x`.

The critical issue: **the GT contains `t*x` and `|v|^(1/3)`**. Let me check which candidates can produce both.

**`t*x` term:** This can come from `x*cos(c*t)` only approximately (via Taylor expansion), but NOT exactly. The term `x*cos(c*t) = x - c²t²x/2 + ...` which is NOT `t*x`. So `x*cos(c*t)` cannot produce `t*x` exactly.

Similarly, `x*sin(c*t)` gives `c*t*x - c³t³x/6 + ...` — not exact either.

**`|v|^(1/3)` term:** This is a fractional power of absolute value. None of the candidates contain `|v|^(1/3)` or any fractional power of v. The candidates have terms like `v`, `v³`, `v²*x`, `log(v²+1)`, `exp(v²)`, `tanh(...)`, etc.

Since the GT requires both `t*x` (which no candidate can produce exactly from the available basis functions) AND `|v|^(1/3)` (which no candidate contains), **no candidate can match the GT exactly**.

Let me verify: Could any candidate somehow produce `|v|^(1/3)`? No — the available v-dependent terms are polynomials in v, `exp(v²)`, `log(v²+1)`, `tanh(...)`, none of which equal `|v|^(1/3)`.

Could `t*x` be produced? The only t*x-like terms come from `x*cos(c*t)` or `x*sin(c*t)` or `x*exp(...)`, none of which are linear in t.

Since both `t*x` and `|v|^(1/3)` are essential non-zero terms in the GT and no candidate can produce either one exactly, no candidate matches.
